       8             :  * JS parser.
       9             :  *
      10             :  * This is a recursive-descent parser for the JavaScript language specified by
      11             :  * "The ECMAScript Language Specification" (Standard ECMA-262).  It uses
      12             :  * lexical and semantic feedback to disambiguate non-LL(1) structures.  It

    4353             : 
    4354             : /*
    4355             :  * Destructuring patterns can appear in two kinds of contexts:
    4356             :  *
    4357             :  * - assignment-like: assignment expressions and |for| loop heads.  In
    4358             :  *   these cases, the patterns' property value positions can be
    4359             :  *   arbitrary lvalue expressions; the destructuring is just a fancy
    4360             :  *   assignment.
    4361             :  *
    4362             :  * - binding-like: |var| and |let| declarations, functions' formal
    4363             :  *   parameter lists, |catch| clauses, and comprehension tails.  In
    4364             :  *   these cases, the patterns' property value positions must be
    4365             :  *   simple names; the destructuring defines them as new variables.
    4366             :  *
    4367             :  * In both cases, other code parses the pattern as an arbitrary
    4368             :  * primaryExpr, and then, here in checkDestructuringPattern, verify
    4369             :  * that the tree is a valid AssignmentPattern or BindingPattern.
    4370             :  *
    4371             :  * In assignment-like contexts, we parse the pattern with
    4372             :  * pc->inDestructuringDecl clear, so the lvalue expressions in the
    4373             :  * pattern are parsed normally.  primaryExpr links variable references
    4374             :  * into the appropriate use chains; creates placeholder definitions;
    4375             :  * and so on.  checkDestructuringPattern won't bind any new names and
    4376             :  * we specialize lvalues as appropriate.
    4377             :  *
    4378             :  * In declaration-like contexts, the normal variable reference
    4379             :  * processing would just be an obstruction, because we're going to
    4380             :  * define the names that appear in the property value positions as new
    4381             :  * variables anyway.  In this case, we parse the pattern with
    4382             :  * pc->inDestructuringDecl set, which directs primaryExpr to leave
    4383             :  * whatever name nodes it creates unconnected.  Then, here in
    4384             :  * checkDestructuringPattern, we require the pattern's property value
    4385             :  * positions to be simple names, and define them as appropriate to the
    4386             :  * context.
    4387             :  */
    4388             : template <>
